# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Controller Manager Work Queue and Rate Limiting

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the controller work queue with rate limiting: the RateLimitingInterface, the ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter, the BucketRateLimiter, and the controller reconcile loop that uses Add/Get/Done for queue management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive search of the Kubernetes codebase for controller work queue with rate limiting components. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've identified all the Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes (v1.32.0) that implement the controller work queue with rate limiting system. The findings include:

**Core Infrastructure Files:**
1. **rate_limiting_queue.go** - Defines `RateLimitingInterface` and `TypedRateLimitingInterface` with AddRateLimited(), Forget(), and NumRequeues() methods
2. **default_rate_limiters.go** - Implements `ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter` (per-item exponential backoff) and `BucketRateLimiter` (token bucket overall rate limiting)
3. **queue.go** - Base queue implementation with the core `Add()`, `Get()`, and `Done()` methods
4. **delaying_queue.go** - Supports delayed item re-queueing

**Controller Examples** showing the reconcile loop pattern:
- Sample controller and 20+ production controllers (Job, ReplicaSet, Node, Service, etc.) all follow the same pattern: `Run()` → `runWorker()` → `processNextWorkItem()` which calls `queue.Get()`, processes the item, calls `queue.Done()`, and on error calls `queue.AddRateLimited()` for backoff-based retry

The results have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol definitions, and a detailed explanation of how these components work together to implement Kubernetes' powerful rate-limited work queue system.

resources\\n69: type Controller struct {\\n70: \\t// kubeclientset is a standard kubernetes clientset\\n71: \\tkubeclientset kubernetes.Interface\\n72: \\t// sampleclientset is a clientset for our own This\\n82: \\t// means we can ensure we only process a fixed amount of resources at a\\n83: \\t// time, and makes it easy to ensure we are never processing the same item\\n84: \\t// simultaneously in \\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n99: \\n100: \\t// Create event broadcaster\\n101: \\t// Add sample-controller types to the default Kubernetes Scheme so Events can be\\n102: \\t// logged for It will block until stopCh\\n160: // is closed, at which point it will shutdown the workqueue and wait for\\n161: // workers to finish processing their current work items.\\n162: func (c *Controller) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int) error {\\n163: \\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\\n164: \\tdefer c.workqueue.ShutDown()\\n165: \\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n166: \\n167: \\t// Start the informer factories to begin populating the informer caches\\n168: \\tlogger.Info(\\\"Starting Foo controller\\\")\\n169: \\n170: \\t// Wait for the caches to be synced before starting workers\\n171: \\tlogger.Info(\\\"Waiting for informer caches to sync\\\")\\n172: \\n173: \\tif ok := cache.WaitForCacheSync(ctx.Done(), c.deploymentsSynced, c.foosSynced); We also must remember to call Forget\\n210: \\t// if we do not want this work item being re-queued. For example, we do\\n211: \\t// not call Forget if a transient error occurs, instead the item is\\n212: \\t// put back on the workqueue and attempted again after a back-off\\n213: \\t// period.\\n214: \\tdefer c.workqueue.Done(objRef)\\n215: \\n216: \\t// Run the syncHandler, passing it the structured reference to the object to be synced.\\n217: \\terr := c.syncHandler(ctx, objRef)\\n218: \\tif err == nil {\\n219: \\t\\t// If no error occurs then we Forget this item so it does not\\n220: \\t\\t// get queued again until another change happens.\\n221: \\t\\tc.workqueue.Forget(objRef)\\n222: \\t\\tlogger.Info(\\\"Successfully synced\\\", \\\"objectName\\\", objRef)\\n223: \\t\\treturn true\\n224: \\t}\\n225: \\t// there was a failure so be sure to report it. This\\n230: \\t// method will add a backoff to avoid hotlooping on particular items\\n231: \\t// (they're probably still not going to work right away) and overall\\n232: \\t// controller protection (everything I've done is broken, this controller\\n233: \\t// needs to calm down or it can starve other useful work) cases.\\n234: \\tc.workqueue.AddRateLimited(objRef)\\n235: \\treturn true\\n236: }\\n237: \\n238: // syncHandler compares the actual state with the desired, and attempts to\\n239: // converge the two. It then updates the Status block of the Foo resource\\n240: // with the current status of the resource.\\n241: func (c *Controller) syncHandler(ctx context.Context, objectRef cache.ObjectName) error {\\n242: \\tlogger := klog.LoggerWithValues(klog.FromContext(ctx), \\\"objectRef\\\", objectRef)\\n243: \\n244: \\t// Get the Foo resource with this namespace/name\\n245: \\tfoo, err := c.foosLister.Foos(objectRef.Namespace).Get(objectRef.Name)\\n246: \\tif err != nil {\\n247: \\t\\t// The Foo resource may no longer exist, in which case we stop\\n248: \\t\\t// processing.\\n249: \\t\\tif errors.IsNotFound(err) {\\n250: \\t\\t\\tutilruntime.HandleErrorWithContext(ctx, err, \\\"Foo referenced by item in work queue no longer exists\\\", \\\"objectReference\\\", objectRef)\\n251: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n252: \\t\\t}\\n253: \\n254: \\t\\treturn err\\n255: \\t}\\n256: \\n257: \\tdeploymentName := foo.Spec.DeploymentName\\n258: \\tif deploymentName == \\\"\\\" {\\n259: \\t\\t// We choose to absorb the error here as the worker would requeue the\\n260: \\t\\t// resource otherwise. It's a read-only, local cache.\\n316: \\t// You can use DeepCopy() to make a deep copy of original object and modify this copy\\n317: \\t// Or create a copy manually for better performance\\n318: \\tfooCopy := foo.DeepCopy()\\n319: \\tfooCopy.Status.AvailableReplicas = deployment.Status.AvailableReplicas\\n320: \\t// If the CustomResourceSubresources feature gate is not enabled,\\n321: \\t// we must use Update instead of UpdateStatus to update the Status block of the Foo resource.\\n322: \\t// UpdateStatus will not allow changes to the Spec of the resource,\\n323: \\t// which is ideal for ensuring nothing other than resource status has been updated.\\n324: \\t_, err := c.sampleclientset.SamplecontrollerV1alpha1().Foos(foo.Namespace).UpdateStatus(ctx, fooCopy, metav1.UpdateOptions{FieldManager: FieldManager})\\n325: \\treturn err\\n326: }\\n327: \\n328: // enqueueFoo takes a Foo resource and converts it into a namespace/name\\n329: // string which is then put onto the work queue.
